      <article class="post-4957 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail hentry category-ecommerce-wordpress category-memberships-plugins category-wordpress has-author-avatar" id="post-4957">
       <header class="entry-header">
        <h1 class="entry-title">
         What is the best WordPress membership plugin for me?
        </h1>
        <div class="entry-comment-count">
         <a href="http://chrislema.com/best-wordpress-membership-plugin/#comments">
          125 Comments
         </a>
        </div>
        <time class="entry-date published" datetime="2014-07-29T23:59:15+00:00">
         July 29, 2014
        </time>
       </header>
       <div class="entry-content">
        <h2>
         <a href="http://chrislemacom.c.presscdn.com/wp-content/uploads/shutterstock_85447960-1.jpg">
          <img alt="Best WordPress membership plugin" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-4958" src="http://chrislemacom.c.presscdn.com/wp-content/uploads/shutterstock_85447960-1-600x400.jpg"/>
         </a>
        </h2>
        <h2>
         Asking the question in the right way
        </h2>
        <p>
         Im not joking that I get this question almost every single day of the year. Last year I can only think of two or three days that I didnt get it. Sometimes it comes in email. Sometimes from my contact page. Other times on Facebook as a chat. And other times in the comments on one of my membership posts.
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          Whats the best WordPress membership plugin for my situation?
         </strong>
        </p>
        <p>
         Its a great question. But this is no longer 2008. We have a lot more choices. So anyone who gives you an answer, directly, without asking you more is doing you a disservice.
        </p>
        <p>
         Because the selection you make
         <em>
          should be based on you
         </em>
         . Not on the features of each plugin.
        </p>
        <p>
         Many have very similar features. Some are written better than others and perform better. Others have better support. Some are easier to use.But that only matters when you need it to matter.
        </p>
        <p>
         So if youre asking someone (not just me) about the best WordPress membership plugin, I want you to stop for a second.
        </p>
        <p>
         Because I dont want you to ask the question in a way that gets you a cruddy answer.
        </p>
        <ul>
         <li>
          Be prepared to explain what you will charge for.
         </li>
         <li>
          Be prepared to explain how much youll charge.
         </li>
         <li>
          Be prepared to explain when youll charge.
         </li>
         <li>
          Be prepared to explain how often you want to charge.
         </li>
         <li>
          Be prepared to articulate what youre protecting.
         </li>
         <li>
          Be prepared to explain what is generic and what is specific to each person.
         </li>
         <li>
          Be prepared to explain whether a person can join more than one level of membership at a time.
         </li>
        </ul>
        <p>
         If youre writing a note, asking this question, youll want to put all of this in there. Because if not, I wont know how best to give you advice.
        </p>
        <p>
         In this quick video, I liken it to how you pick the next couch you buy.
        </p>
        <p>
         <iframe allowfullscreen="allowfullscreen" frameborder="0" height="315" src="//www.youtube.com/embed/Ps7nTvdQXzo?list=PLVVWU1aYx2Xh5mVEYQ7DqF8KMgUuh8l-m" style="line-height: 1.5em;" width="560">
         </iframe>
        </p>
        <h2>
         So, do you have this question?
        </h2>
        <p>
         Are you wondering which one to select? Maybe you dont even know which ones are out there.
        </p>
        <p>
         There are many, but I only like to highlight the ones that are really well-written and supported well. I know that means that some of the ones youve heard of (from way back when) may not be listed below, but thats on purpose.
        </p>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="http://chrislema.com/cart66" target="_blank">
           Cart66
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="http://chrislema.com/exchange" target="_blank">
           Exchange
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="https://memberful.com/" target="_blank">
           Memberful
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="http://chrislema.com/membermouse" target="_blank">
           MemberMouse
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="http://chrislema.com/memberpress" target="_blank">
           MemberPress
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="http://chrislema.com/pmp" target="_blank">
           Paid Memberships Pro
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="http://chrislema.com/rcp" target="_blank">
           Restrict Content Pro
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="http://www.woothemes.com/products/groups-woocommerce/" target="_blank">
           WooCommerce
          </a>
          +
          <a href="http://wordpress.org/plugins/groups/" target="_blank">
           Groups
          </a>
          +
          <a href="http://www.woothemes.com/products/woocommerce-subscriptions/" target="_blank">
           Subscriptions
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
        <p>
         Now, to be clear, those 8 options are ordered by their names, not my preference.
        </p>
        <p>
         Why? Because how can I have a preference, or recommendation for you, without knowing more about your situation.
        </p>
        <p>
         So tell me  what business are you trying to run? Give me the details. Ill see if theres a good option for you, from the list above.
        </p>
        <p>
         <span itemprop="video" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/VideoObject">
          <meta content="What is the best WordPress membership plugin for me?" itemprop="name"/>
          <meta content="http://chrislemacom.c.presscdn.com/wp-content/uploads/jpg52" itemprop="thumbnailURL"/>
          <meta content="Wondering how to decide which is the best WordPress membership plugin? Asking a more detailed and nuanced question will help you get an answer." itemprop="description"/>
          <meta content="2014-01-13T13:21:00+00:00" itemprop="uploadDate"/>
          <meta content="https://www.youtube-nocookie.com/v/Ps7nTvdQXzo" itemprop="embedURL"/>
          <meta content="http://www.youtube.com/v/Ps7nTvdQXzo?version=3&amp;f=videos&amp;app=youtube_gdata" itemprop="contentURL"/>
          <meta content="PT3M5S" itemprop="duration"/>
         </span>
        </p>

               <p>
                Weird that you actually say this Jason because no where on your website is there a phone number for contact. Ive looked everywhere and you provide no number.  I too have sent you questions via your online form and never heard back. That was weeks ago. Add to that the fact that your pricing plans are severely lacking in any specifics as to what they offer and a couple actually contradict each other. For someone who does website development, Im kinda surprised at how badly you guys communicate your pricing structure. There are a number of weird issues with PMP but one of the worst is the shipping information plugin you suggest using and that you guys authored. On your website it says Adds Shipping Address fields to the membership checkout page, confirmation page, confirmation emails, members list and edit user profile pages. Not one confirmation email had any shipping info on it and in fact, when you enter shipping info upon checkout, that information isnt even SAVED in the database. I went back to the PMP Admin page to check and sure enough, no member profiles had any shipping info saved. At this point, Im bailing on using PMP you guys kinda leave a bad taste in my mouth.
               </p>

        <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 comment-parent" id="comment-10194">
         <article class="comment-body" id="div-comment-10194">
          <header class="comment-header">
           <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-38 photo" height="38" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/2d41ca18346ec2a31268ccd44d899cec?s=38&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/2d41ca18346ec2a31268ccd44d899cec?s=76&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g 2x" width="38"/>
           <div class="comment-date">
            <a href="http://chrislema.com/best-wordpress-membership-plugin/#comment-10194">
             <time datetime="2014-01-13T16:09:58+00:00">
              January 13, 2014 at 4:09 pm
             </time>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="comment-author vcard">
            <cite class="fn">
             <a class="url" href="https://plus.google.com/102467330535757397514" rel="external nofollow">
              Scott Roberts
             </a>
            </cite>
            <span class="says">
             says:
            </span>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content">
           <p>
            To answer the questions in your post:
           </p>
           <p>
            1) access to post content
            <br/>
            non-members see teaser content on some posts, full content in others
            <br/>
            free &amp; paid members have full post access
           </p>
           <p>
            2) access to enhanced video assets  particularly HD streams (via LiveStream and/or Vimeo, maybe YouTube streaming once Im eligible)
            <br/>
            day pass: 99 cents (non-recurring)
            <br/>
            monthly (recurring) pass: $2.49 (discounted to $1.49 first month)
            <br/>
            yearly (recurring) pass: $10.99  (7 day free trial)
           </p>
           <p>
            3) monthly and yearly accounts have additional access  archives, photo galleries, etc.
           </p>
           <p>
            4) EOT on paid memberships, the account reverts to free access level, not guest access.
           </p>
           <p>
            5) Each member has a personal home page  in the style of a static site home page with widgets. Yearly members have media posting rights.
           </p>
           <p>
            6) There is a free membership level not advertised directly on the site. This has category-limited full posting privileges (its for emergency managers in each county of Kansas)
           </p>
           <p>
            7) The site is eventually going to be the content back-end for a mobile app.
           </p>
           <p>
            Ive tried S2member, didnt get there with it. Im using WP eMember on another site; too heavy, difficult and slow for this site. THought about Justin Tadlock and Pippins member plugins but didnt feel the feature sets were there within my budget. I started working it with Paid Memberships Pro yesterday, and it seems like Ill get where I want to be with it.
           </p>
           <p>
            Would you agree, or is there something lurking there I havent considered?
           </p>
          </div>
          <footer class="comment-reply">
           <a aria-label="Reply to Scott Roberts" class="comment-reply-link" href="/best-wordpress-membership-plugin/?replytocom=10194#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "div-comment-10194", "10194", "respond", "4957" )'>
            Reply
           </a>
          </footer>

            <header class="comment-header">
             <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-38 photo" height="38" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/fc98dc7b6690c7a987a779e4f06e763f?s=38&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/fc98dc7b6690c7a987a779e4f06e763f?s=76&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g 2x" width="38"/>

             <div class="comment-author vcard">
              <cite class="fn">
               <a class="url" href="http://www.paidmembershipspro.com" rel="external nofollow">

             </div>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content">
             <p>
              Nathan, you are asking Chris, but weve helped people set this up with Paid Memberships Pro. Here is a code gist and tutorial for hiding old content from members.
              <a href="http://www.paidmembershipspro.com/2011/09/hide-old-posts-from-new-members/" rel="nofollow">
               http://www.paidmembershipspro.com/2011/09/hide-old-posts-from-new-members/
              </a>
              And here is the code gist for non-PMPro-members
              <a href="https://gist.github.com/4066459" rel="nofollow">
               https://gist.github.com/4066459
              </a>
             </p>
             <p>
              That code can easily be adjusted to allow members to view all content and restrict access to content older than 2 weeks for non-members. If you need help setting it up, open a member support ticket at
              <a href="http://www.paidmembershipspro.com" rel="nofollow">
               http://www.paidmembershipspro.com
              </a>
              and well get the code for you.
             </p>

        <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1" id="comment-10208">
         <article class="comment-body" id="div-comment-10208">
          <header class="comment-header">
           <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-38 photo" height="38" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/0c2042e2d58a25ade173f3ef07eb22b6?s=38&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/0c2042e2d58a25ade173f3ef07eb22b6?s=76&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g 2x" width="38"/>

             </time>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="comment-author vcard">
            <cite class="fn">
             Jan
            </cite>
            <span class="says">
             says:
            </span>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content">
           <p>
            Nice overview of available options.
           </p>
           <p>
            Can you comment on the
            <a href="http://wordpress.org/plugins/participants-database/" rel="nofollow">
             Participants Database
            </a>
            plugin?
           </p>
           <p>
            I use it to control the membership of a club of people, mostly to manage the registration information needed. It also allows the members to manage this information by themselves.
           </p>
           <p>
            Maybe Im wrong and this plugin doesnt even belong in this membership plugin list, but it might also be that it is not on this list because of another reason I dont know of.
           </p>
          </div>

            <div class="comment-content">
             <p>
              I suggest you look outside WP for something like this.  I presume that a degree of document security, etc. would be pretty important.  Something like Yammer Enterprise ($3/month/user) would work, and there are others.  You can set up highly segregated groups, and since I assume that most condo associations wouldnt have more than 4 or 5 board members, the cost per property would be quite reasonable at $12-$18 per month total.
             </p>

          <div class="comment-content">
           <p>
            Our club is looking to move away from a standalone membership product (Memberties) and move to an integrated solution with our WordPress site.
           </p>
           <p>
            We run a club where membership is yearly and members can buy anywhere from one to 10 years in advance.
           </p>
           <p>
            Wed like members be able to service and update their account information themselves.
           </p>
           <p>
            Wed like members to be able to be reminded that their dues are upcoming and then process their own payments.
           </p>
           <p>
            Subscription type abilities would be nice for the long time users.
           </p>
           <p>
            We DO NOT care about content protection almost all of the membership products we have looked at are geared towards this arena thats fine but something we dont care about.
           </p>
           <p>
            we have approx 1700 members and associated spouses brings it to around 3000+
           </p>
           <p>
            Does ANYONE know of a product that would be inline with what we are looking for Price isnt too much of a concern a stable product and support are what matters to us. Think tennis club, yacht club, country club thats the type of membership management were looking for.
           </p>
           <p>
            Thanks Gang!

          <div class="comment-content">
           <p>
            Hi Chris,
           </p>
           <p>
            Heres what Im looking to do and I havent been able to accomplishing this with RCPro, PMPro, s2member, Membership by mpmudev, User Access Management or PrivateContent (Code Canyon). The only plugin Ive found that was able to achieve all of my needs out-of-the-box is Memberpress:
           </p>
           <p>
            1. Password protect a single page with an image on it for free.
            <br/>
            2. This image needs to be on a page which cannot be accessed by anyone whos not logged in.
            <br/>
            3. Once they register and/or login, they should be able to view the image and then logout of the site with ease.
            <br/>
            4. I dont want Subscribers to have access to the admin bar or the WordPress Dashboard, I only want users to see the front end of the site.
            <br/>
            5. Any email sent from the plugin shouldnt have WordPress as the sender, I should easily be able to change this to whatever I want such as the name of my website.
            <br/>
            6. The registration form needs to be editable and I should be able to add or take away as many fields as I want at will.
           </p>
           <p>
            My question is, do you think Cart66, Exchange, Memberful, MemberMouse, Magic Members, or WooCommerce+Groups are capable of achieving all of these tasks? Please let me know your thoughts.
           </p>
           <p>
            Cheers
           </p>

          <li class="comment byuser comment-author-chrislema bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 comment-parent" id="comment-10634">
           <article class="comment-body" id="div-comment-10634">
            <header class="comment-header">
             <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-38 photo" height="38" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/282d599b414022eba5096510f675b6e2?s=38&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/282d599b414022eba5096510f675b6e2?s=76&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g 2x" width="38"/>
             <div class="comment-date">
              <a href="http://chrislema.com/best-wordpress-membership-plugin/#comment-10634">
               <time datetime="2014-02-01T17:59:52+00:00">
                February 1, 2014 at 5:59 pm
               </time>
              </a>
             </div>
             <div class="comment-author vcard">
              <cite class="fn">
               <a class="url" href="http://chrislema.com" rel="external nofollow">
                chrislema
               </a>
              </cite>
              <span class="says">
               says:
              </span>
             </div>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content">
             <p>
              I think all the membership plugins you mentioned will let you do the following:
             </p>
             <p>
              1. Create a membership role.
              <br/>
              2. Let people register for it, for free.
              <br/>
              3. Protect a page so that only those members can see it.
              <br/>
              4. Place an image on that page.
             </p>
             <p>
              Thats what membership plugins do. Ive used Cart66, Exchange, Memberful, MemberMouse, WooComerce+Groups and MemberPress to do all of that.
             </p>
             <p>
              The emails that get sent by your site arent completely in the control of membership plugins. Thats to say that some go an extra mile to give you additional control. Others dont. But that doesnt mean you cant control who sends it.
             </p>
             <p>
              For example, I use SendGrids mail service and I control who the outbound name/domain is that sends it. To do that, I use this plugin:
              <a href="http://wordpress.org/plugins/wp-mail-smtp/" rel="nofollow">
               http://wordpress.org/plugins/wp-mail-smtp/
              </a>
             </p>
             <p>
              And my membership plugins respect that. So if you ask them about email control, you may get an answer that doesnt sound right, but its because what youre asking for (actual delivery) is often outside the scope of their plugin.
             </p>
             <p>
              As for access to the backend of WordPress, again, some plugins do this, others dont. Some give you control over hiding it (like WooCommerce+Groups, MemberPress, etc) while others may not worry about it.
             </p>
             <p>
              Why wont they worry about it? Because there are other plugins that can control that. The theme youre seeing here is that WordPress plugin developers want to deliver a complete solution, but everyone has differing needs, so if that feature already exists in another plugin, they may stay clear of it. Or work with it.
             </p>
             <p>
              Justin Tadlock created a content protection plugin (Members  not on your list, but also does this stuff) and I used to use this plugin (
              <a href="http://wordpress.org/plugins/wp-hide-dashboard/" rel="nofollow">
               http://wordpress.org/plugins/wp-hide-dashboard/
              </a>
              ) in combination with Members to protect the dashboard.
             </p>
             <p>
              Now, even if a member could see the admin bar and/or dashboard, you should know that changing that can be just a couple lines of code (already available online) to add to your theme that limits all subscriber roles from seeing the admin bar.
             </p>
             <p>
              Alternatively, this plugin (
              <a href="http://wordpress.org/plugins/wp-admin-no-show/" rel="nofollow">
               http://wordpress.org/plugins/wp-admin-no-show/
              </a>
              ) does exactly what you want, regardless of which membership solution you choose.
             </p>
             <p>
              Lastly, you would like additional registration fields. Again, some plugins do this as part of their membership solution. Many do. But some dont.
             </p>
             <p>
              In the case of those that dont, this $59 plugin does it, plus handles the admin bar, etc (
              <a href="http://www.cozmoslabs.com/wordpress-profile-builder/" rel="nofollow">
               http://www.cozmoslabs.com/wordpress-profile-builder/
              </a>
              ).
             </p>
             <p>
              Now, your question was a question about out of the box. And I guess my best answer to you is simply this.
             </p>
             <p>
              No membership plugin will do everything you want, perfectly just for you, without you doing any work at all, out of the box. None. Theyre all amazing. Theyre all great. But membership sites are a multi-billion dollar industry. And every different site wants things different. So if youre getting into the space, be prepared to do a tiny bit of work.
             </p>
             <p>
              All said, a site that does what you want, with the existing plugins listed in your list, plus maybe one of the ones Ive mentioned here, could create your solution in a couple of hours. But often by someone who knows how WordPress, and these plugins, work.
             </p>
             <p>
              If youre new to this, your best bet is great questions like the one above, that encourage people to get you good answers.
             </p>
            </div>
            <footer class="comment-reply">
             <a aria-label="Reply to chrislema" class="comment-reply-link" href="/best-wordpress-membership-plugin/?replytocom=10634#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "div-comment-10634", "10634", "respond", "4957" )'>
              Reply
             </a>
            </footer>

           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content">
           <p>
            Chris,
           </p>
           <p>
            I have a site that draws 30k views per month and 4-5k podcast downloads. I am interested in protecting content with free and paid memberships. The main thing I would like to do is tease registration through partial content on a post so that a free membership is required to see the full article. I would like to protect some podcasts in this way as well. I am not as interested in registration pages and welcome pages. I want the visitor who is in the middle of a post to be able to register for free very quickly, without them ever leaving the page, preferably with an ajax login/registration. I love login-with-ajax but I have already found that it conflicts with s2 Member. Also, I am using WP Supercache because otherwise the site is too slow on my shared server, so I would love an ajax solution that will work with a cached site setup.
           </p>

            Appreciate any advice or tips anyone has.

           </p>

            This is what Im doing;
           </p>
           <p>
             My membership site is directed towards company owners/managers and their clients.  It provides them with high quality, highly valuable occupational health &amp; safety documentation, presentations, alerts and Im also starting a forum for members.
           </p>
           <p>
             There are three levels Basic $49.99 Comprehensive $79.99 and Premium $129.99 all per month.  However, given the quality and amount of documentation, the full annual fee is charged up front before membership is granted.
           </p>

             Recurring charges are annual using Paypal
           </p>
           <p>
             The major difference between membership levels is the type and amount of documentation. For example the Basic package will only have access to PDF versions of manuals, etc.  The comprehensive will have access to some Word docs but some still remaining in PDF.  The Premium will be all native files access to everything.  Because of this, there will be no requirement for members to have access to more than one level of membership at a time.
           </p>
           <p>
            Any direction is greatly appreciated.

           </p>
           <p>
            I am developing an investment real estate site that will require public pages/posts/content (no login required), semi-private pages/post/content (registration and login required) and private pages/content viewable by the one login they are assigned to. All memberships are free.
           </p>
           <p>
            What would you recommend?
           </p>
           <p>
            Thanks for all the great info. C. Marshall Smith (Chris)
           </p>
          </div>

          </header>
          <div class="comment-content">
           <p>
            Ive got one for you
           </p>
           <p>
            I run a volunteer-powered group that teaches kids to code. We dont want to charge for memberships. Instead we want to use them as a marketing tool to make it easier for users to sign up for our events and for us to communicate with them.
           </p>
           <p>
            Part of this is creating two classes of membership Family and Individual. A parent would have to sign up for a family membership, which would in turn create their individual membership. They could then register for submemberships for their children (which they could have control over) and spouse (which they wouldnt).
           </p>
           <p>
            This could then be integrated with an event management system that would let us control the number of adult and child tickets being reserved. It would also give them a reservation form for an event where theyd just check off which members of the family are attending.
           </p>
           <p>
            We dont need e-commerce in the ticketing system or the membership system.
           </p>
          </div>

          <div class="comment-content">
           <p>
            First site Ive done here, so Id appreciate some guidance.  Im selling a series of video modules (9 currently, more to be developed).  Each module has 5-9 videos.
           </p>
           <p>
            A person can sign up for any one module for $3, and should be able to purchase additional modules on their account.  Access will be granted for 4 months from the date of the most recent module purchased.  They can also get the whole series for 4 months for $15, with a deluxe membership for $25 giving them lifetime access (this option will also give access to new modules as produced).

           </p>

        <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 comment-parent" id="comment-36020">
         <article class="comment-body" id="div-comment-36020">
          <header class="comment-header">
           <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-38 photo" height="38" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e5cfdacc89186d2d39051f4397671cc7?s=38&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/e5cfdacc89186d2d39051f4397671cc7?s=76&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g 2x" width="38"/>
           <div class="comment-date">
            <a href="http://chrislema.com/best-wordpress-membership-plugin/#comment-36020">
             <time datetime="2014-06-27T06:43:56+00:00">
              June 27, 2014 at 6:43 am
             </time>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="comment-author vcard">
            <cite class="fn">
             <a class="url" href="http://gravatar.com/louisecuschieri" rel="external nofollow">
              Louise Cuschieri
             </a>
            </cite>
            <span class="says">
             says:
            </span>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content">
           <p>
            Hi,
           </p>
           <p>
            Im a bit desperate to find a plugin which will do what I need, which is not all that complicated, but the two that Ive tried extensively dont want to play nicely.
           </p>
           <p>
            1. Site is open to all visitors  its a blog site with news articles. Visitors can see only excerpts, members will see the full article (by use of
            <!--more-->
            tag or similar.
           </p>
           <p>
            2. Everyone has access to all areas of site, no restricted pages, just restricted in content on the pages.
           </p>
           <p>
            3. Subscriptions are a 30 day free trial  we do NOT want members to part with their credit card number at this stage.
           </p>
           <p>
            4. After the free trial we want members to be promoted  via email before expiry  that their free trial is expiring and to click on link to subscribe for paid subscription.
           </p>
           <p>
            5. Payments via PayPal single payments and PayPal Express. Eventually using recurring billing and enhanced recurring billing. Must have option for members to pay with PayPal account but also with a credit card without having to create PayPal account.
           </p>
           <p>
            6. Tried WPMU DEV Membership plugin. Problem is a weakness in their subscription plan set-up whereby either a member can keep signing up for a free trial OR their free trial will expire within them being notified.
           </p>
           <p>
            7. Tried Magic Members plugin. Looked promising in all the areas that WPMU DEV was not covering, but lacks basic protection options. Their philosophy is: protect everything by default and enable what you want. My site is the exact opposite: I want everything available, except certain content. Consequently using their manual tags of [private][/private] (like the more tag) this works fine for pages and articles but NOT for category listings. There is no way to enable this using their protect everything philosophy.
           </p>
           <p>
            8. Need to be able to edit communication emails.
           </p>
           <p>
            9. Need to be able to edit the text message that will be displayed instead of the protected content.
           </p>
           <p>
            10. I have spent months trying to customise WPMU DEV however their latest update changed the philosophy in their access levels as well, so am tearing my hair out once again.
           </p>
           <p>
            What can you recommend?
           </p>
           <p>
            Thanks,
            <br/>
            Louise
           </p>
          </div>
          <footer class="comment-reply">
           <a aria-label="Reply to Louise Cuschieri" class="comment-reply-link" href="/best-wordpress-membership-plugin/?replytocom=36020#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "div-comment-36020", "36020", "respond", "4957" )'>
            Reply
           </a>

            <header class="comment-header">
             <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-38 photo" height="38" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/282d599b414022eba5096510f675b6e2?s=38&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/282d599b414022eba5096510f675b6e2?s=76&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g 2x" width="38"/>
             <div class="comment-date">
              <a href="http://chrislema.com/best-wordpress-membership-plugin/#comment-36054">
               <time datetime="2014-06-27T08:17:52+00:00">
                June 27, 2014 at 8:17 am
               </time>
              </a>
             </div>
             <div class="comment-author vcard">
              <cite class="fn">
               <a class="url" href="http://chrislema.com" rel="external nofollow">
                chrislema
               </a>
              </cite>
              <span class="says">
               says:
              </span>
             </div>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content">
             <p>
              Many of the plugins will do what you want  but youll need to tweak things. Paid Memberships Pro is flexible if youre looking to code tweaks, or have them do it. Restrict Content Pro and Exchange, along with MemberPress, all take PayPal. Notifying your members 25 days after signup, to invite them to sign up is a custom trigger that isnt hard, but not normally included with plugins.
             </p>
            </div>

        <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-51202">
         <article class="comment-body" id="div-comment-51202">
          <header class="comment-header">
           <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-38 photo" height="38" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/9dc0d496b12ded6d6a4296d9d8620209?s=38&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/9dc0d496b12ded6d6a4296d9d8620209?s=76&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g 2x" width="38"/>
           <div class="comment-date">
            <a href="http://chrislema.com/best-wordpress-membership-plugin/#comment-51202">
             <time datetime="2014-08-11T16:10:00+00:00">
              August 11, 2014 at 4:10 pm
             </time>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="comment-author vcard">
            <cite class="fn">
             SandyFischler
            </cite>
            <span class="says">
             says:
            </span>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content">
           <p>
            I was looking for exactly this type of information!
           </p>
           <p>
            What we will charge for:
            <br/>
            User will create their own sub-site with their own pages using our theme. Think Pinterest, Facebook, or any other social site with a user profile and content (vanity URL under our URL).
            <br/>
            <a href="http://www.oursite/joesmith/mypage1" rel="nofollow">
             http://www.oursite/joesmith/mypage1
            </a>
            for example.
           </p>
           <p>
            How much we will charge:
            <br/>
            Pricing not set yet but were looking at anywhere from $10 monthly to $30 monthly depending on how our final feature packages play out and how much content were going to store. Other features might include a CRM, calendar, ability to have multiple pages under the vanity URL, analytics.
           </p>
           <p>
            When/how often we will charge:
            <br/>
            Monthly and yearly subscriptions. There will be some kind of free trial offer.
           </p>
           <p>
            What are we protecting:
            <br/>
            Each user should be able to access only their own content, no access to the site admin or any other users account/content.
           </p>
           <p>
            Generic/Specific:
            <br/>
            Theme is generic (fonts, colors, header, footer). Specific to each person is the exact content and  layout details on where specific content blocks land within the page. For example, someone with an image heavy content set will want a slightly different layout than someone with a text heavy content set. The Theme we want to use is
            <a href="http://my.studiopress.com/themes/news/#demo-full" rel="nofollow">
             http://my.studiopress.com/themes/news/#demo-full
            </a>
            and each user should be able to organize the layout to their preference. The user should literally have their own CMS as part of the account so they can organize and manage their content.
           </p>
           <p>
            Join more than 1 level of membership:
            <br/>
            No.
           </p>
           <p>
            Any input would be fantastic to help us narrow down the right plugin.
           </p>
           <p>
            Thanks!
            <br/>
            Sandy
           </p>
          </div>
          <footer class="comment-reply">
           <a aria-label="Reply to SandyFischler" class="comment-reply-link" href="/best-wordpress-membership-plugin/?replytocom=51202#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "div-comment-51202", "51202", "respond", "4957" )'>
            Reply
           </a>
          </footer>

          <header class="comment-header">
           <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-38 photo" height="38" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/8d9f31257fb609bc065255ed687f47e0?s=38&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/8d9f31257fb609bc065255ed687f47e0?s=76&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g 2x" width="38"/>

             <time datetime="2014-11-19T14:43:33+00:00">
              November 19, 2014 at 2:43 pm
             </time>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="comment-author vcard">
            <cite class="fn">
             Panda
            </cite>
            <span class="says">
             says:
            </span>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content">
           <p>
            Hi Chris,
            <br/>
            Thank you for the post and you are absolutely right! Ive been searching and deciding and then undeciding on many of the plugins mentioned and even ones not on the list. Currently, I narrowed it down to two but am undecided. Here is my list of must haves:
           </p>
           <p>
            1. MUST allow us to choose between Authorize.net ARB and Authorize.net AIM (we currently have AIM and my boss is unsure if he will do ARB). Paypal to us is icing on the cake. Stipe also.
           </p>
           <p>
            2. Must give managers power to make changes on the backend in an intuitive way and prompt the admin when changes are made to user profiles(Addresses, exp date, membership level, etc.). User can update parts of profile also and this will also prompt the admin.
           </p>
           <p>
            3. Creates invoices and behaves a lot like a cart on the backend, including powerful reporting.
           </p>
           <p>
            4. Comes with drip, pay per post, pay per download, trial, and regular subscription modules.
           </p>
           <p>
            5. Must have Mailchimp integration and autoresponders.
           </p>
           <p>
            6. Gives us a choice to integrate BuddyPress or bbPress.
           </p>
           <p>
            7. Partial content display, download protection and post protection.
           </p>
           <p>
            Theres more, but these are what stands out in my mind at the moment. Thank you.
           </p>
          </div>

           </p>
           <p>

           </p>

If not a signed in subscriber we would like our visitors to be redirected to a registration page (or a popup) when they click on an article (Category)
           </p>
           <p>
             some pages will also need to free to view at all times (contact page etc.)
           </p>
           <p>
            Thanks in advance, Tom
           </p>
          </div>

          <header class="comment-header">
           <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-38 photo" height="38" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a9d76e9433a401ed1d69f6312f5b83b8?s=38&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g" srcset="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a9d76e9433a401ed1d69f6312f5b83b8?s=76&amp;d=blank&amp;r=g 2x" width="38"/>
           <div class="comment-date">
            <a href="http://chrislema.com/best-wordpress-membership-plugin/#comment-134468">
             <time datetime="2015-02-05T12:55:01+00:00">
              February 5, 2015 at 12:55 pm
             </time>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="comment-author vcard">
            <cite class="fn">
             <a class="url" href="http://www.northoakcliffpatrol.com" rel="external nofollow">
              Jerry Beech
             </a>
            </cite>
            <span class="says">
             says:
            </span>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content">
           <p>
            We alrady use WordPress currentl for our own website
            <a href="http://www.northoackcliffpatrol.org" rel="nofollow">
             http://www.northoackcliffpatrol.org
            </a>
            .  We are a non profit membership based community organization of 450 paid members, and 2500 potential members (potential houses) and our organization uses membership money to hire off duty police officers to patrol our neighborhood..  We are interested in maintaining a database of the memberships and non members (all are based on street address).
           </p>
           <p>
            We would like to create a system where the members can go online and update their personal information (such as their contact information, family members, emergency contacts, etc. and pay for a 6 or 12 month long membership.   Currently members mail forms to us and we enter their updated information  manually, which is a page long and very tedious, and often there is a delay between when they send in their information and when we have it updated.    It would be nicer if members could update their stuff online at any time and make payments online that get immediately credited to them.
           </p>
           <p>
            We do not have content we need to protect on our web site, except for possibly one page.
            <br/>
            Members only see their own information, and this must be protected as it is confidential
            <br/>
            Members need a way to login using their address as their id, and a way to recover password if they have forgotten it via email.  We typically have email addresses for two spouses so iot needs to be able to be recovered for the primary member and the spouses email address, as they MUST share a membership record..  New members would just get blank information page they could fill out and create their own password.
            <br/>
            We would like members to be able to buy a membership for 6 months or 12 months that gets auto charged to them via credit card or ACH on a monthly basis.  Right now they have to pay full 6-12 months in advance as it is too hard for us to process monthly payments.
            <br/>
            We would love to be able to have their membership auto-renew at the end of the term, unless they request otherwise.
            <br/>
            Finally, we have 12 volunteer staffers who need to be able to go into and modify membership data as needed, and we need to be able to create a PDF or other html report of the membership information online  that our police officers can access easily with the current membership data and membership status (including our non member addresses).
           </p>
           <p>
            Any suggestions on a membership plugin for WordPress that would be able to be used for this would be greatly appreciated.  We have fairly limited financial resources so need a system that is inexpensive, but fairly experienced wordpress users who can do Java, PHP or ASP as needed to make minor tweaks, but the system needs to be continued without a lot of maintenance.
           </p>
           <p>
            Thank you so much!!
           </p>
          </div>

            <div class="comment-content">
             <p>
              Ive been using PMPro for about a year now on a clients project &amp; they have absolutely AMAZING support.  Bar none best Ive come across.  The caveat here is that when using PMPro, youre gonna need that support unless you are fluent with PHP.  The plugin is really cool in regards to its ability to basically do anything you want it to.  But the tricky (and extremely frustrating) aspect of that is even the most minor tweaks require php knowledge.  But like i said, the paid support forum is great &amp; the mods on there do a fantastic job with helping with these minor things.
              <br/>
              But personally, Ive started using Membermouse on another clients project and like it much better.  The smart tag functionality makes the dev workflow run much smoother considering you dont need to hard code every nuance you need when it comes to specific access rights, content display, etc.
             </p>
            </div>
